I wanted to Thank everyone at Kindred for helping me recover from my tracheostomy which was a necessity after two intubations and CPAP/ Bipap not allowing my CO2 levels to normalize. I was very nervous at first and just having had to be tube fed with no voice, Patricia (nurse) made me comfortable right away with her upbeat sweetness. Learning how to care for a trach can be a process but luckily I had several good RT‚Äôs (respiratory therapists) to help. Heather was always offering knowledge and was quick to help out, Tiffany was thorough and watchful when I was afraid to try CPAP again ‚Äî she checked on me several times to make sure I was comfortable. Johanna was so encouraging even when I had a couple of hard days. Patrick took his time to answer all of the questions (which there were many).  I love Luis‚Äôs sense of humor and he was very upbeat. My original trach was too big:hence, the speak valve and eating/swallowing were out of the question until it was changed. Luis changed it with his partner in seconds making the process very easy. I have to say being bed bound at the beginning was not fun for me but Rosa, Rich, Bree along with many other nurses really helped me feel more dignified and took great care of me. I even got my hair washed which is very difficult with a new trach.   Henoch was extremely good with IV‚Äôs and NG tubes. Lupe was so quick, responsive and helped me greatly with everything from paperwork to mundane duties. She made a huge difference in my last few days at Kindred. My speech therapist ,Jojo,  was also very good: she made sure it would be safe to eat, drink before I started. She looked at my history and did tests accordingly.  I also could barely sit up when I first got to Kindred. Debra (my occupational therapist) first got me standing as well my physical therapists: Janice and Cesar after one week. Pretty soon we were standing and then walking. My other occupational therapist, Lauren, came back and she trained me on self care so I could go home. The doctors at this hospital are fantastic. Dr. Phan is so thorough and brilliant. His analysis of my blood work took care of problems I have had for over a year! Dr. Sandu whom performed my surgery (with Dr. Abudali another wonderful doctor) would follow up every other day on recovery status. Dr. Houramy is an extremely empathetic,spiritual, and sharp pulmonologist who came in with inspiring words frequently. He also really listened to my concerns and treated me accordingly. I absolutely thought the Infectious disease specialist Dr. Guiang was very thorough (of course) to make sure all the pneumonia was gone and she also came in with encouragement every day. Of course my patient advocates and case workers helped me greatly as well. Thank you Lisa, Mary, Lorilyn and Cindy!! Thanks to all of these people, I was able to come home, have a smooth transition. I am off oxygen at times and walking without any help at times (this is my 2nd day home). I am starting to do more and more for myself. <Review>Six months ago I had LANAP laser surgery with Dr. Colleran for some very advanced periodontal issues that the periodontist I had seen told me were untreatable and would end up in the loss of three teeth. Although I won't know for sure for another six months when they do the 1 year probing checkup, I am fairly certain those teeth are no longer at risk. I have no more bleeding or pus. I would strongly urge anyone with periodontal disease to try the LANAP before doing any of the old fashioned surgeries that I had done that only made things worse. I had my entire mouth done in one long session, and within two weeks felt relatively normal. Dr. Colleran's office had messed up the date of service and my claim had been denied. After multiple calls, time, and stress, we were able to get it sorted out and I 'only' owed about $150.

I had begun to get the feeling that they were doing a lot of unnecessary work, but again, I stupidly kept going. During my last 'hygiene' appointment, they took x-rays and had the dentist come look at my teeth. I thought I was there for a standard hygiene appt, but apparently they did a bunch of 'extras' without checking with me ahead of time.  Following that appointment, I received a bill for $300.

When they called me to set up and appointment for additional work, I told them I wouldn't be coming back because they were too expensive.

I haven't had enough time to follow-up with them about the bill, so it has sat unpaid. When I called today, they told me that the hygienist should have checked with me ahead of time. She didn't.  Since I had already told them that I would not be returning due to excessive costs, they insist that I pay the full bill even though they screwed up.

I will be paying it, but I think it's important that other people know the way this office does business. Expect to be told you need fillings, mouth guards, or other work every single time you come in. Do not expect to be told of costs before receiving service. And most importantly, be prepared to pay out of pocket (above and beyond a co-pay) for each visit.<//review><Pictures>None< /Pictures><resp>{'time': 1463092491050, 'text': 'Thank you for your honest review. < review>
With everyone trying to stay busy and maintain social distancing while adhering to new standards during this pandemic, also people eager to quarantine and find creative ways to pass the time,  one would think that the store would be better stocked and cleaner and maybe  the employees could be a little kinder and possibly more helpful. I couldn't find anyone to help me locate an item. All the employees seemed to be huddled up near the front registers, lounging or lazily picking through some boxes. There was no hustle, and the staff didn't seem to be in any hurry to unpack whatever was on the boxes so I don't know why no one was on the floor. When o asked for the item in question, I was told by one of the employees that they were out, they then asked another to confirm this and the response was "yeah, we're out" then they went back to their lounging,  shuffling and sorting. No word on when item would be back in stock, no offers to find a comparable or replacement item. I wandered around the disorganized mess and found something comparable myself, except that it was missing the price tag..I was asked if I knew how much the item cost, and then asked where I found it and if there were anymore. I ended up leaving the item on the counter and walking out. I get that everyone is stressed at this time, but this was an absolute effort to be that unhelpful.  I ended up purchasing the original item I wanted at Walmart.</review>

<review>Michaels can be a little more on the pricey side of craft stores, but they almost ALWAYS have coupons and/or sales going on! I literally just purchased 17 canvas from them for $30 when it would typically have cost me $60. As an avid painter that is a pretty sweet deal! Plus at the end of holiday seasons,  they do grab bags of what is left. These grab bags are usually $4 and filled to the brim with seasonal items. Its a great way to prepare for next year without paying full price! You wont always love every single thing in the bags, but I love the mystery of not knowing what is inside!<//review>< Response>
